ÔÇ NO ÔÇ NO OPINION Hyperlinks are references to data that lead a user from one location in the Internet to another. They are indispensable for the functioning of the Internet as a network. Severalcasesare pending before the CJEUin which the question has been raised whether the provision of a¬ clickable link constitutes an act of communication to the public/making available to the public subject to the authorisation of the rightholder. A user browsing the internet (e.g. viewing a web-page) regularly creates temporary copies of works and other subject-matter protected under copyright on the screen and in the 'cache' memory of his computer. A question has been referred to the CJEUas towhether such copies are always covered by the mandatory exception for temporary acts of reproduction provided for in Article 5(1) of Directive 2001/29/EC.

ÔÇ YES ‚ÄìPlease explain howsuchpotential effectscould beaddressed There is no need to clarify the territorial scope of the ‚Äúmaking available‚Äù rights. However, we do believe that there is a need to ensure a better implementation of Article 8.3 of the Copyright Directive. Pan-European injunctive reliefs should work effectively in practice, as each Member State shall take any and all measures necessary to ensure that rights holders whose interests have been affected by an infringing activity carried out on its territory can bring an action for damages and/or apply for an injunction and, where appropriate, for the seizure of infringing material. EU Member States shall ensure that rights holders are in a position to apply for an injunction against intermediaries whose services are used by a third party to infringe a copyright or a related right. This may complicate the licensing of worksfor online use notably when the two rights are held by different persons/entities.

ÔÇ YES ‚ÄìPlease explain howsuchpotential effectscould beaddressed The rather large number of cases brought to the courts asking what exactly constitutes "making available" is a sign that this important term is not sufficiently clear. Technologies like embedding and framing, cultural practices like compiling and remixing are likely to grow their social and economic importance. A principled and technology neutral definition of "making available" is needed. ‚Ä¶‚Ä¶‚Ä¶‚Ä¶‚Ä¶‚Ä¶‚Ä¶‚Ä¶‚Ä¶‚Ä¶‚Ä¶‚Ä¶‚Ä¶‚Ä¶‚Ä¶‚Ä¶‚Ä¶‚Ä¶‚Ä¶‚Ä¶‚Ä¶‚Ä¶‚Ä¶‚Ä¶‚Ä¶‚Ä¶‚Ä¶‚Ä¶‚Ä¶‚Ä¶‚Ä¶‚Ä¶‚Ä¶‚Ä¶‚Ä¶‚Ä¶. ‚Ä¶‚Ä¶‚Ä¶‚Ä¶‚Ä¶‚Ä¶‚Ä¶‚Ä¶‚Ä¶‚Ä¶‚Ä¶‚Ä¶‚Ä¶‚Ä¶‚Ä¶‚Ä¶‚Ä¶‚Ä¶‚Ä¶‚Ä¶‚Ä¶‚Ä¶‚Ä¶‚Ä¶‚Ä¶‚Ä¶‚Ä¶‚Ä¶‚Ä¶‚Ä¶‚Ä¶‚Ä¶‚Ä¶‚Ä¶‚Ä¶‚Ä¶. Each act of transmission in digital networks entails (in the current state of technology and law) several reproductions. This means that there are two rights that apply to digital transmissions: the reproduction right and the making available right. This may complicate thelicensing of works for online use notably when the two rights are held by different persons/entities.

The rather large number of cases brought to the courts asking what exactly constitutes "making available" is a sign that this important term is not sufficiently clear. Technologies like embedding and framing, cultural practices like compiling and remixing are likely to grow their social and economic importance. A principled and technology neutral definition of "making available" is needed. Each act of transmission in digital networks entails (in the current state of technology and law) several reproductions. This means that there are two rights that apply to digital transmissions: the reproduction right and the making available right. This may complicate the licensing of works for online use notablywhen the two rights are held by different persons/entities.

If such rights, for example, could be licensed by any of the Copyright socities within the E.U., then the useres would turn to the Society with the cheapest rates. BUT: rights owner will then withdraw their rights from any "cheap rate" Copyright Societyand give their European Copyrights to the one Society with the highest rates. There is NO competition within theCopyright market because noone would license a certain Copyright because it is cheaper instead of the one he actually wants. It is comparableto concert tickets. Noone would say: "I would not attend a Lady Gaga concert because it is too expensive. I would rather go to a no Name concert which costs not even 10% of Lady Gaga's concert." People want to enjoy the Kind of Music they want and they arewilling to pay the Prices. Any Kind of competition between the Copyright Societies would, in the second round, lead to a massive increase in license fees and the Establishment of a monoploy Copyright Socities. This may complicate the licensing of works for online use notably when the two rights are held by different persons/entities.

ÔÇ YES ‚ÄìPlease explain howsuchpotential effectscould beaddressed I am not aware of practical problems regarding the definition of ‚Äúauthorship‚Äù in the EU with regard to ‚Äúmaking available‚Äù. A ‚Äúcountry of origin‚Äù rule would substantially weaken the usefulness of the right. The right is most useful when an infringement action can be brought against someone who does not make an unauthorised reproduction in a territory but has done so or assisted/facilitated the making of the copy in another jurisdiction. The fact that the exceptions to copyright infringement regarding reproduction are not co-extensive with the exceptions for making content available is also useful in practice. ÔÇ YES ‚ÄìPlease explain howsuchpotential effectscould beaddressed If a ‚Äúclarification‚Äù is seen as implementing a ‚Äúcountry of origin‚Äù principle, this would be in contradiction with general principles of copyright and the objective to safeguard a high level of protection forright holders. Anti-piracyenforcement against services made available either in other EU countries or in third countries would be seriously impeded if such offers could not be fought against in the very markets where such service is not originating from, but where it is accessible and accessed. A different approach would seriously harm right holders, who then could not fight services having a serious negative economic impact on licensed services. Quite to the contrary, this would support anonymous infringers. Each act of transmission in digital networks entails (in the current state of technology and law) several reproductions. This means that there are two rights that apply to digital transmissions: the reproduction right and the making available right. This may complicate the licensing of worksfor online use notably when the two rights are held by different persons/entities.
